Let's verify again with lsblk. Type in sudo space lsblk space dash f and hit enter. We can now see that it's formatted as ext3. You can go back and forth between these two formats without losing data. The ext2 and the ext3 file system drivers will go away in future versions of the [Linux](../../Skills/Network%20and%20System%20Administration/Linux.md) kernel. The newer ext4 driver can mount an older drive for backwards compatibility. To show how to use ext4 driver to mount an ext2 or ext3 drive, just pass the ext4 file system as an argument to the mount command. Type in clear and then type in sudo space mount space dash t space ext4 space slash dev slash vgdata slash lvdata... ...space and then the mount point is slash media slash lvdata and hit enter. Now let's verify this with df space dash capital T. Dash capital T instructs df to show the file system type. Type in sudo space df space dash capital T and hit enter.
>
> **[3:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/lpic-1-exam-101-version-5-0-cert-prep/create-ext-filesystems?u=76281980&t=187)** We can see that the file system is mounted as ext4. The thing to remember is that mounting an older drive like this works but the file system isn't really ext4, it's just using the ext4 driver in the kernel. Mounting a drive like this does not take advantage of the new features in ext4.

#### [Repair EXT filesystems](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/lpic-1-exam-101-version-5-0-cert-prep/repair-ext-filesystems?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/lpic-1-exam-101-version-5-0-cert-prep/repair-ext-filesystems?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] It's inevitable that your file system will need to be repaired at some point. We're going to use our lv data logical volume for this exercise. In order to fix the file system, we need to break it first. Let's begin by copying files to our amounted volume. Make sure that lv data is mounted on /media/lvdata. If it is not, then mount it. Type in sudo, space, mount, space, /dev/vgdata/lvdata, space, /media/lvdata. And hit enter. We can verify this with df. Now let's copy a bunch of files to it. For this exercise, it does not matter which files, so we'll just copy / to it. Type in clear, and then type in sudo, space, cp, space, /, capital R, lowercase vf, space, /media/lvdata and hit enter. Let that go for a while and then kill it by pressing control+c. We need a lot of files in the file system so we have a higher chance of corrupting one of them. Now that we have files, let's cause some chaos. You don't have to unmount it for this, because we're actually trying to cause problems. We'll use dd to copy data from /dev/0 to random places on the file system. We'll run this multiple times and change the seat value. If this does not create corruption on your system, try different numbers and keep going until you get a corrupted file system. Type in clear and then type in sudo, space, dd, space, if=/dev/zero, space, bs=1, that's the block size,
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/lpic-1-exam-101-version-5-0-cert-prep/repair-ext-filesystems?u=76281980&t=96)** space, count=10, that's 10 blocks, space, of=/dev/vgdata/lvdata, space, seek=1000.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/lpic-1-exam-101-version-5-0-cert-prep/repair-ext-filesystems?u=76281980&t=112)** This is where we'll start writing data. And hit enter. Bring your line back and change the seek to something else, like 1200. Bring it back again and change it to something else again.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/lpic-1-exam-101-version-5-0-cert-prep/repair-ext-filesystems?u=76281980&t=130)** Do this four or five times with different numbers. Now unmount the volume and run a file system check on it. Type in clear and then type in sudo, space, umount, space /media/lvdata. And hit enter. Now to run a file system check, type in sudo, space, fsck, space -n, space, /dev/vgdata/lvdata. And hit enter. If you have corruption, it'll show an error message on the screen. If you do not, go back to the previous step and try a bunch of different seek numbers. Now that we know we have corruption, let's talk a moment about fsck. There are several different options we might want to be aware of. Fsck, space -capital A checks all file systems. Fsck, space -capital A, capital R checks all file systems except for the root file systems. Fsck, space -f checks file systems even if they are considered clean. Fsck space -a fixes safe problems automatically. These are issues that don't need review from an administrator. Fsck space -y answers all questions with a yes. Be very careful with this. There are some decisions that need an administrator to make. For instance, if the drive suddenly has thousands of errors, maybe it's actually a [Hardware](../../Topics/Hardware.md) problem. If so, trying to copy all data from the drive is probably a better use of our time than attempting to fix the file system itself when it may not be the problem.
>
> **[3:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/lpic-1-exam-101-version-5-0-cert-prep/repair-ext-filesystems?u=76281980&t=222)** Fsck space -n doesn't fix anything, it just displays the results. This is what we just did. Now let's go back to our terminal and fix our file system. Type in clear, then type in sudo, space, fsck, space, /dev/vgdata/lvdata. And hit enter. When it prompts you to fix each error, it will tell you what is wrong. Press y. If there are a lot of errors, we can do fsck space -y. Press control+c, bring your line back and do fsck space -y and hit enter. Once it's done, run it a second time to see if the file system is clean. If it is, you're done. Since it's a bad idea to check file systems that are mounted, it's difficult to check the root file system. Watch the video in this course on logical volume snapshots for one solution. You can create a snapshot, run the file system check on the snapshot to see if there are any errors. If there are, you can then make a decision to take the operating system offline to fix it, which will require a reboot.

#### [Basic features of Btrfs](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/lpic-1-exam-101-version-5-0-cert-prep/basic-features-of-btrfs?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/lpic-1-exam-101-version-5-0-cert-prep/basic-features-of-btrfs?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Narrator] In the past, the job of dividing up drives and then formatting them was handled by two separate processes. Drives were divided up using partitions or logical volume management and then the volumes were formatted with a file system such as EXT4 or XFS using a different set of tools. If you needed to create or repair partitions, you'd use partition tools. If you needed to create or repair logical volumes, you use LVM tools, and if you needed to create or repair file systems, you'd use tools specific to the type of file system you're using. There are different tools for EXT-based file systems, XFS file systems, and so on. A new era in file systems has begun and one could argue that it started with Sun Microsystems' ZFS file system. In 2005, Sun Mircosystems released a file system called ZFS. ZFS is a file system but has many features traditionally found on disk partitioning tools, such as pooled storage, copy-on-write, snapshots, [Data Integrity](../../Skills/Cybersecurity/Data%20Integrity.md) verification and automatic repair, and RAID-Z which is a unique, dynamic disk striping system. ZFS enlarged parts of Sun Solaris were opensourced. Oracle bought Sun Microsystems in 2010 and played ZFS under a closed source license. Many of the developers left and started OpenZFS. A couple of years before Oracle bought Sun Microsystems and the code for ZFS, one of their developers started working on a new advanced file system called Btrfs or Btrfs. Btrfs was scheduled to be released in 2008 and was added to the [Linux](../../Skills/Network%20and%20System%20Administration/Linux.md) kernel in 2009 right before Oracle bought Sun Microsystems.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/lpic-1-exam-101-version-5-0-cert-prep/basic-features-of-btrfs?u=76281980&t=92)** In 2012, two distributions moved Btrfs to production status, Oracle Linux and Suse Enterprise server. However, Redhat in 2017 announced they were no longer planning to migrate to Btrfs and it has been removed from Redhat Enterprise Linux 8. This shouldn't be looked at as a sign of problems for Btrfs. Btrfs has taken longer to mature than expected and Redhat doesn't currently employ any Btrfs engineers so they can't support it. Btrfs has many advanced features that cross the same line between partitioning tools and file system tools as ZFS does. I'm not going to go into how a B-Tree file system like Btrfs works as it can get quite complex and that is beyond the scope of this course, however, Btrfs features include support for copy-on-write and is mostly self healing. It has online resizing of volumes, online adding and removing of block devices, online balancing or moving of objects between block devices to balance load. Online searching and repairing of errors for files that have redundant copies and support for RAID 0, RAID 1, and RAID 10 as well as subvolumes or multiple volumes in one partition. It also supports transparent compression per file or volume, atomic writable snapshots and read-only snapshots, file cloning, checksums on data and [Metadata](../../Skills/Web%20Development/Metadata.md), incremental backups, data de-duplication, and lastly support for swap files and partitions. Notice some of these features sound like a more traditional file system like XFS and some of these features are currently handled by the Linux Raid Layer or LVM.
>
> **[3:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/lpic-1-exam-101-version-5-0-cert-prep/basic-features-of-btrfs?u=76281980&t=186)** There are a few features like transparent compression and data de-duplication that are not supported using traditional methods in Linux. File systems can be complex and when entered the realm of the ZFS and Btrfs types of file systems they can get very complex. As such, this is just a quick overview of what Btrfs is and what it can do.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>
> **Frameworks & Libraries:** [Linux](../../Skills/Network%20and%20System%20Administration/Linux.md) (5), [Data Integrity](../../Skills/Cybersecurity/Data%20Integrity.md) (1), [Metadata](../../Skills/Web%20Development/Metadata.md) (1)
> **Env Vars:** zfs (8), raid (4), xfs (3), lvm (2), ext4 (1)
> **Definitions:** is a  (2)
> **Analogies:** such as (2)

With other operating systems such as [Windows](../../Glossary/Service/Windows.md), we might use the ZIP tool for this. In [Linux](../../Skills/Network%20and%20System%20Administration/Linux.md), we use and Archiver, to preserve [Metadata](../../Skills/Web%20Development/Metadata.md) such as ownership, permissions, access control lists, as well as the file data itself. The tool we usually use is TAR, or Tape Archiver. TAR itself doesn't compress files, but leaves that job up to the compression tools. TAR doesn't compress archives itself, but has the ability to call on external compression tools. #### [Taking the exam](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/lpic-1-exam-101-version-5-0-cert-prep/taking-the-exam?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/lpic-1-exam-101-version-5-0-cert-prep/taking-the-exam?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Grant] The LPIC-1 Version 5 certification is made up of two exams. This course covers exam 101. For this exam, time management is key. You have roughly 60 questions to accomplish in 90 minutes, but the minutes can go by fast. The exam consists of multiple choice and fill-in-the-blank questions. Complete the easy questions first. If you get hung up on one difficult item and run out of time before getting to the easier items, you may fail the test. The test really does follow the exam objectives. The [Linux](../../Skills/Network%20and%20System%20Administration/Linux.md) Professional Institute has told you what is on the exam so pay close attention to the objectives. This exam has increased focus on [System Architecture](../../Skills/Software%20Development/System%20Architecture.md), Linux installation and [Package Management](../../Skills/Web%20Development/Package%20Management.md), GNU and Unix commands, devices, Linux filesystems, and the filesystem hierarchy standard. Each LPI exam is ranked on a scale from 200 to 800 with a passing score of 500. Since exam questions vary in difficulty, the number of correct answers required to reach the passing score of 500 will depend on the exact combination of questions on the exam you take. For security purposes, candidates are not always given the same questions as one another for a particular exam. The exam passing score is based on LPI's psychometric studies to ensure all exams have a consistent level of difficulty. The number of questions is also tied to the total of the weights for the objectives on the exam. This exam has a total weight count of 60. As such, the exam has 60 questions. For each weighting, there will be one question. For example, Objective 102.2, install the boot loader, has a weight of two.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/lpic-1-exam-101-version-5-0-cert-prep/taking-the-exam?u=76281980&t=91)** This means there will be two questions on the exam related to this objective. For objective weighting, see the exam objectives. As of this recording, the price of the exam is 200 US Dollars and there are no prerequisites for taking the exam. Keep in mind that the technologies and commands listed in the objectives in this course may not be exhaustive. LPI reserves the right to change the test as they see fit. Lastly, practice, practice, practice. Walk through this course more than once, complete the assessment questions more than once without using [Google](../../Glossary/Service/Google.md) or your notes, and good luck.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>
> **Frameworks & Libraries:** [Linux](../../Skills/Network%20and%20System%20Administration/Linux.md) (3), [System Architecture](../../Skills/Software%20Development/System%20Architecture.md) (1), [Package Management](../../Skills/Web%20Development/Package%20Management.md) (1), [Google](../../Glossary/Service/Google.md) (1)
> **Env Vars:** lpi (3), lpic (1), gnu (1)
